The Ministry of Finance Has Formulated Regulations for Handling Smuggled Goods 111

The Ministry of Finance has now formulated nine articles of regulations for handling smuggled goods seized by its subordinate anti-smuggling agencies, in order to facilitate their handling and avoid disputes. They are recorded as follows: (Article 1) The customs, taxation, and salt anti-smuggling agencies under the Ministry of Finance shall, in addition to assisting each other as much as possible in anti-smuggling matters, handle the confiscation and rewards of all smuggled goods seized from each other in accordance with these regulations. (Article 2) Smuggled goods (including smuggled salt) and criminals seized by anti-smuggling agencies that are not under the jurisdiction of their own agency shall be sent to the nearest competent agency for handling in accordance with regulations. However, if the seized smuggled salt is dirty, of poor quality, unfit for consumption, or cannot be sold, the seizing agency shall notify the nearest salt agency to send personnel to destroy it if necessary. In addition, if the seized imported smuggled goods require the payment of both customs duties and taxes under the jurisdiction of the Tax Affairs Department, they shall be sent to the customs for handling in places where customs are established, and to the tax office in places where customs are not established. The handling agency shall consult with the relevant agencies before handling the above items, and the handling agency shall inform the relevant agencies of the handling situation for verification. (Article 3) The means of transporting public or private smuggled goods, such as ships, aircraft, vehicles, livestock, etc., shall be handled by the seizing agency in accordance with regulations depending on the circumstances. (Article 4) All agencies that send the seized smuggled goods and criminals to the nearest competent agency in accordance with Article 2 of these regulations shall receive reimbursement for all expenses actually incurred, such as shipping costs, by presenting formal receipts to the nearest competent agency. (Article 5) All money confiscated or sold from the smuggled goods and criminals sent by the seizing agency to the nearest competent agency in accordance with regulations shall be distributed in the following proportions after deducting the expenses reimbursed in Article 4 and the expenses incurred during the sale: 40% for the treasury, 30% for the personnel who seized the goods, and 30% for the delivery to the treasury. The proportion to be received by the informant and the personnel involved shall be paid by the handling agency after receiving the money. If there are fines, they shall also be handled in the same way, unless there are special regulations for customs and taxation (such as smuggled cigarette paper), in which case this article shall not apply. (Article 6) No bonuses shall be given for smuggled goods that cannot be sold due to damage or special reasons, or for dirty, poor-quality smuggled salt that is unfit for consumption and should be destroyed in accordance with Article 2. Article 8 does not apply in this case. (Article 7) If smuggled goods cannot be sold, all expenses that should be allocated according to Article 4 shall still be requested by the handling agency for separate reimbursement. (Article 8) If the personnel who seized the smuggled goods have made special contributions and need to be rewarded generously, and the seized goods cannot be sold, the handling agency shall request a separate reward. (Article 9) These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Taxpayer Association Regular Executive Committee Meeting to Discuss Solving Telephone Problems, Suggestions from Electrical Appliance Industry and Other Guilds 113

Although the telephone problem in the special district has reached a stalemate due to the company's stubbornness, all sectors feel deeply affected and public opinion continues to criticize without hesitation. The Taxpayer Association of the concession has regularly convened an executive committee meeting to seek a solution. Yesterday, the Electrical Appliance Industry, Wire and Iron Machinery Industry, and other guilds sent a letter to the Special District Telephone Committee, suggesting three ways to deal with the problem. The original text is recorded below:

To the Telephone Problem Committee from various guilds such as the Telephone Industry: With respect, the Shanghai Telephone Company, in this difficult commercial time, changed the new telephone charging regulations, disregarding the public opinion of all citizens, and resolutely implemented them. Although your committee and other representatives of the citizens have tried their best to protest, the effect is minimal. All members of our guilds are part of the citizens and are all telephone users. We are willing to be a strong backing for the enthusiastic protests of your committee and offer our humble opinions to your committee as a basis for continued negotiations. We hope for your wise decision. We present our opinions in detail below. Upon investigation, the only reason for the Shanghai Telephone Company's change of regulations is to achieve an annual interest rate of 10%. According to the internal organization of the company obtained by our guilds, the company still cannot achieve an annual interest rate of 10% even after the price increase. There are several reasons for this: A. The basic major shareholder of the company is a certain American telephone company. B. The company uses new telephones and other materials, all of which are supplied by a certain American telephone company, and the price exceeds the market price. (Please ask the committee to find a way to investigate this price.) C. The Shanghai Telephone Company's profit cannot reach an annual interest rate of 10% because this profit has already been taken away by a certain American telephone company. Therefore, the Shanghai company cannot directly obtain an annual interest rate of 10%, but it has been indirectly taken away by the major shareholder, a certain American telephone company. In the future, when the company purchases telephone materials, it should determine the type of goods the company needs, formulate procedures, and invite merchants to bid, so that the lowest price can be obtained. In this way, the company can also make a profit. Stopping payment is not a fundamental solution for continued negotiation and it is difficult to achieve final victory. The reason is that the method of stopping payment has been adopted in the past, but the company uses the method of breaking through individually, and the result is almost zero. For example, if 100 users stop paying, the company will disconnect the lines of 10 of these 100 non-paying users, and the remaining 90 users can still make calls even if they do not pay. Therefore, the 10 households whose lines are disconnected will inevitably panic and feel inconvenienced. After insisting for a few days, they feel that the negotiation is still ineffective, so they have to pay and ask for the phone to be reconnected. After the company waits for the 10 households whose lines are disconnected to pay, it will disconnect the lines of another 10 households among the other 90 households. Following the above method, it will be applied to the remaining non-paying users one by one. Therefore, although there are many users in Shanghai, they are broken through one by one. Therefore, our guilds feel that this method of stopping payment is difficult to be effective. To continue the protest, we must be determined to sacrifice. The first step is to dismantle the telephones: A. Organize a telephone dismantling opportunity, send personnel to various industry guilds and citizen district branches to contact them, and convene a general meeting within three days. The user affiliated with the various industries, and users who have a relationship with various personal users, the responsible party of the meeting should be the various industry guild to host, and other personal users who do not belong to various industries should be hosted by the civic association. B. Users must fill in a letter of commitment to dismantle the telephone and store it in the respective groups. C. Each user should write a letter to the telephone company in advance, stating that they request the company to dismantle the telephone immediately, and attach a statement that if the telephone is not dismantled after the deadline, the user will cut the line themselves, and the user will not be responsible for any fees or damage losses. The letter must be signed and sealed and stored in each of the organizing groups. If necessary, the organizing groups may send the letter to the Shanghai Telephone Company on their behalf. The above methods are within the scope of our guilds' humble opinions. We hope that your committee will study them in detail and inform us accordingly. We hope for your consideration and a reply.

Taxpayer Association: The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Public Concession issued a notice yesterday, which reads: With respect, it is scheduled to hold the seventh executive committee meeting at 4:00 p.m. on Wednesday, March 15, in the upstairs hall of our association at 59 Hong Kong Road. We hope that you will take the time to attend the meeting on time to discuss the telephone issue. Respectfully issued.

Fishermen in Wanhai Petition the Ministry of Finance to Improve the Color Change of Salt Used for Fish Preservation and Request to Use Rice Bran Instead 114

According to the Shin Shi News Agency, the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association received a letter from representatives of fishermen in Daishan, Dinghai County, stating that the Liangzhe Salt Transport Envoy of the Ministry of Finance, in order to prevent government and private salt from being mixed and resold, ordered the fishermen in the area to mix red soil or coal dust into the salt used for pickling fish and crabs in order to identify it. This method affects the color of the fresh fish, and customers who are unaware may easily misunderstand it, mistaking the fresh fish for rotten fish, which is a major concern for the livelihood of the fishermen. Therefore, they requested the Ministry of Finance to change the method and offered suggestions for adoption. After receiving the letter, the association sent separate letters to the Ministry of Finance, the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and the Liangzhe Salt Transport Envoy yesterday, which read: With respect, according to the representatives of fishermen in Daishan, Dinghai County, Han Xiangzhou, Huang Jun, Zhao Changwei, Zhou Peifu, etc., in recent years, the economic downturn has spread throughout the country, and the social economy has undergone drastic changes. All industries are declining, especially the fishing industry. For example, in the past, fishermen could sell the fish and crabs they caught for 100 yuan, but now they can only sell them for 40 or 50 yuan, and sometimes no one even asks about them. At a time when fishermen are struggling to survive, the government suddenly issued an order to change the color of salt used for fishing, ordering fishermen to mix red soil into the salt used for pickling fish and crabs to make the salt red, or mix coal dust to make it gray. The original intention was nothing more than to identify government and private salt and prevent mixing and reselling. However, those who buy fish and crabs in the market judge the freshness of the fish based on their appearance and set the price accordingly. The freshness of the fish depends on the scales and gills. White scales are considered fresh and sell for a higher price, while black scales are considered stale and unfit for consumption. As for red, it is not suitable. For example, dried fish that are originally white will turn red or gray when they are moldy and taste astringent. Now, the fresh and delicious fish and crabs are dyed with colored salt, which customers misunderstand as rotten. All goods will inevitably be unsalable, which will not only affect the livelihood of the fishermen, but also reduce the country's tax revenue. The representatives grew up in the fishing area and have a better understanding of the situation. They cannot bear to see hundreds of thousands of fishermen sit and wait for death. After research, they have found a method that does not violate the law and does not affect the quality of the fish, which is to mix rice bran into the salt used for fishing to make the salt slightly yellow. This can both identify the salt used for fishing and not affect the color and taste of the fish. Fishermen will naturally be happy to comply. Compared with mixing red soil or coal dust to change the color, which is both labor-intensive and affects hygiene, this method has many advantages and no disadvantages. At a time when the fishing industry is declining, the government is paying more attention to protecting it. Weighing the pros and cons, it seems that it should be adopted. Therefore, we briefly state the reasons for changing to using rice bran to mix with fishing salt, and sincerely request your association to present it to the government on our behalf. Please consider the difficulties of the people and allow the change to be made in order to maintain the fishing industry and benefit the people's livelihood. etc. After investigation, the association found that the color and taste changes caused by mixing red soil or coal dust with salt for pickling fresh fish do affect sales, which is indeed the case. Based on the above situation, we are specially presenting it on behalf of the fishermen. We sincerely hope that you will consider it, issue an order for implementation, and maintain the fishing industry. We will be deeply grateful. This is addressed to Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, Chairman Huang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and the Liangzhe Salt Transport Envoy.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Sends a Telegram Requesting Correction of Stamp Tax Inspectors' Abuse of Power in Sending Penalties 117

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, based on a letter from the Straw Hat Industry Association, sent a telegram yesterday to the Ministry of Finance requesting correction of stamp tax inspectors' intentional fault-finding, unwarranted demands, and abuse of power in sending penalties. The telegram read: "To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, (omitted above). According to the regulations in the tax exemption column of the stamp tax rate table and the Ministry's tax document No. 7298, workers' wage account books used to collect wages are exempt from stamp tax. The document also states that 'If workers other than employees of a store receive wages or remuneration, and the store issues account books for them to collect their wages, these account books can be handled accordingly.' Therefore, regardless of whether an industry has a business license or not, if workers in straw hat-making shops, that is, those who work at home, use account books to collect their wages, they are exempt from stamp tax according to the Ministry's above-mentioned instructions. The model of the rental books issued by the Public Security Bureau has been submitted to the Ministry for review. According to the Ministry's tax document No. 8254 of December 31 of last year, the lease agreement on the first page should be affixed with a stamp worth two cents. However, two points should be supplemented: The rental book is issued by the Public Security Bureau once a year, and its validity period is only twelve months. However, the lease is signed after moving into a new house, and its validity continues until moving out or increasing/decreasing the rent or revising a new lease. It is not revised every twelve months. Therefore, tenants are legally not required to affix a stamp to the lease agreement every year. According to the law, stamp tax should be affixed to leases with a monthly rent of ten yuan or more. However, according to the inspectors' claim, it seems that all leases, regardless of the monthly rent, must be affixed with a stamp worth two cents, which is also obviously inconsistent. As for the rental book of the Public Security Bureau, a piece of paper called a rent ticket is cut off each month when collecting rent, which is different from the method used in inland areas outside Shanghai, where rent is collected annually and stamp tax is affixed to the books. Therefore, according to the Ministry's tax document No. 8254, since each receipt has been stamped, the booklet should not be stamped again according to Article 12 of the Implementing Rules of the Stamp Tax Law. The inspectors have repeatedly made unwarranted demands and abused their power in sending penalties for the above two items of account books and rental books, and the court has also imposed penalties without knowing the previous cases, which is inevitable. We request that the Ministry provide a thorough explanation and issue a notice for compliance to avoid merchants suffering injustice again. According to Article 12 of the Implementing Rules of the Stamp Tax Law, check stub books do not need to be stamped. Although check have been temporarily exempted from stamp tax, the application of Article 12 of the Implementing Rules remains unchanged. We also request that the Ministry verify and instruct for compliance. If the loose-leaf receipts are for sending money or goods, they should be affixed with a total of two cents each year. If the content of the invoice stub is completely the same as the first copy given to the customer, because it is a duplicate, or if the content is simpler than the copy given to the customer, it is also used for internal audit. According to Article 3, Clause 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, it is not necessary to stamp them. There is no doubt about the above two items according to the law, and we have already provided answers to the association. However, in order to avoid inspectors intentionally finding fault, we still request that the Ministry provide a combined reply for reference. Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Respectfully."

Executive Committee Member of the National Medical Association, Yang Yanhe, Researches the Results of Insects and Purple Gromwell 122

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Industry Association previously sent a letter to the National Medical Association, asking for identification of the authenticity of ground beetles and false blister beetles, and the differences between purple gromwell root and purple gromwell velvet, and attached four medicines to the association. After deliberation by the National Medical Association, "it was sent to medical groups and executive and supervisory committee members of the association for research, opinions were collected, and then discussed." Mr. Yang Yanhe, a member of the executive committee of the association, sent a letter yesterday to the National Medical Association with the results of his research, which read: "With respect, I have received your letter and a book on the identification of ground beetles and false blister beetles, and the identification of purple gromwell root and purple gromwell velvet. Ground beetles are indeed false blister beetles. The herbal classic already has clear records and medical books can be used to verify each other (such as Wu Youke's Treatise on Pestilential Diseases, which uses Sanjia Powder to treat "principal and secondary pathogens," explicitly stating false blister beetle, while Xue Shengbai's Treatise on Damp-Heat Diseases, which treats "principal and secondary pathogens combined," imitating Wu Youke's Sanjia Powder, directly writes ground turtle beetle, which can be used for mutual verification). However, the pharmacy must not prepare other insects to impersonate ground beetles. The main question has been resolved. As for the purple gromwell velvet, Xie Yuqiong's Complete Book for Saving Lives in Ma Ke states, 'Purple gromwell velvet is formed by the ants on the dragon's blood tree gathering its fat and liquid, which is no different from bees making honey. The one from the True Wax Kingdom is the best, and the one from the Persian Kingdom is the next best. It treats wounds, collapse and leakage, breaks up blood stasis, promotes muscle growth, and stops pain. The world now uses it exclusively to treat pox because it has the effect of activating blood and promoting swelling without the harm of being salty and cold and causing diarrhea. Its effect is twice that of purple gromwell, so it is called purple gromwell velvet, but it is not the same type as purple gromwell.' When Yanhe read this book before, he added a brief note on the eyebrow, saying, 'Purple gromwell velvet is originally the tender stem of purple gromwell, while the purple gromwell velvet recorded by Xie is actually purple mineral.' Based on Xie's records and the records in the Herbal Materia Medica, True Secrets of Pox Learning, Divine Response Heart Book, and the Purple Fish Article in the Compendium of Materia Medica, they are in agreement. The Chinese Medical Dictionary clearly states in the Purple Mineral Article, 'Purple mineral is produced in the Southern Barbarians. It is a kind of small insect like ants and lice that gather its fat and liquid on tree branches to form, colored purple and shaped like mineral stones. When broken open, it is red and transparent like amber. It treats pox and has the effect of activating blood and promoting swelling without the effect of being cold, salty, and causing diarrhea. Its effect is twice that of purple gromwell.' The doubt of Zhao Xuemin, who said, 'According to Ye Dachun, it seems to be purple mineral, but there is no definite explanation,' has been resolved. Therefore, doctors who write prescriptions for measles can draw 'tender purple gromwell,' while those who write prescriptions for pox must change the writing to 'like purple mineral' or 'purple mineral velvet' to avoid unclear entanglement. Please also ask the association to send a circular to medical groups all over the country to inform members, and also send a letter to the Chinese Medicine Industry Association to inform colleagues all over the country to follow the same procedure to avoid misunderstandings, which is really a blessing for patients."

Bank Note Acceptance Center: Detailed Rules for Accepting Bank Notes, Methods for Evaluating, Inspecting, and Storing Collateral, and Procedures for Member Banks to Apply for Bank Note Acceptance 129

Since the establishment of the Bank Note Acceptance Center, it has been almost a week, and applications for accepting bank notes have been quite enthusiastic. However, some industrial and commercial enterprises have not yet understood the application and procedures. Therefore, we have extracted the operating rules of the center for reference.

Acceptance of Bank Notes

Chapter I: General Provisions

Article 1: These detailed rules are formulated in accordance with Article 31 of the Articles of Association of the Bank Note Acceptance Center (hereinafter referred to as "the Center") of the Joint Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Banking Association (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee").

Article 2: The Center shall handle matters related to the acceptance of bank notes in accordance with these detailed rules, in addition to the provisions of the Articles of Association.

Article 3: Notices from the Center to member banks shall be in the form of circulars.

Chapter II: Acceptance of Bank Notes

Article 4: Each member bank shall, in accordance with the acceptance limit determined by the Executive Committee of the Committee, enter into an acceptance contract with the Center.

Article 5: After a member bank has entered into an acceptance contract with the Center, it may, at any time, in accordance with the conditions stated in the contract, issue a list of acceptance collateral for review by the Center. After the Center's review is qualified and the value is assessed, the member bank shall deposit the designated acceptance collateral into the Center, and then fill out an acceptance application form and issue a draft to request the Center's acceptance.

Article 6: All items in the collateral submitted by the member bank that should be transferred or registered shall be endorsed and transferred or registered to the Center by the original submitting bank. If the acceptance collateral needs to be insured, the insurance policy shall designate the Center as the beneficiary.

Article 7: The acceptance fee shall be collected by the Center from the issuing bank each time an acceptance is decided.

Article 8: The accepted bank notes shall be in a specific format prescribed by the Center.

Inspection of Collateral

Chapter III: Inspection of Acceptance Collateral

Article 9: The Center shall conduct a thorough inspection of the acceptance collateral provided by the member bank.

Article 10: The inspection of acceptance collateral shall be carried out in accordance with the following methods:

1. The Center entrusts member banks and other companies or organizations to conduct the inspection on its behalf.

2. The Center dispatches personnel to conduct the inspection.

3. The Center temporarily hires experts to conduct the inspection.

Article 11: The personnel conducting the inspection shall issue two copies of the inspection form, one original and one duplicate, when inspecting the Center's acceptance collateral. The original copy shall be sent to the manager and forwarded to the collateral evaluation group of the Bank Note Acceptance Center Committee, and the duplicate copy shall be filed by the Center for future reference.

Evaluation of Collateral

Chapter IV: Evaluation of Acceptance Collateral

Article 12: The Center shall conduct a thorough evaluation of the acceptance collateral provided by the member bank.

Article 13: The evaluation of acceptance collateral shall be carried out in accordance with the following methods:

1. The collateral evaluation group of the Bank Note Acceptance Center Committee assesses the value.

2. The evaluation committee of the Committee assesses the value.

3. The Center temporarily hires experts to assess the value.

Article 14: When members of the evaluation committee and experts believe that it is necessary to review the original documents or obtain samples of the goods for the evaluation of acceptance collateral, they may request them from the Center.

Article 15: After the members of the evaluation committee and experts have assessed the value, they shall issue two copies of the valuation form, one original and one duplicate. The original copy shall be sent to the original submitting bank through the Center, and the duplicate copy shall be filed by the Center for future reference.

Safeguarding Collateral

Chapter V: Safekeeping of Acceptance Collateral

Article 16: The Center shall keep the acceptance collateral provided by member banks in the Center, except for goods deposited in warehouses.

Article 17: The warehouses where the Center deposits acceptance collateral are divided into the following two types:

1. Member bank warehouses.

2. Non-member bank warehouses.

Article 18: Under any of the following circumstances, a location shall not be used as a place for depositing the Center's acceptance collateral:

1. Adjacent to factories with hazardous materials.

2. Within a military fortress area.

3. In a low-lying area prone to flooding.

4. Not meeting the underwriting standards of the insurance industry.

5. Other unsafe environments.

Article 19: In addition to complying with the Shanghai Banking Industry Warehouse Operating Rules, when the Center deposits acceptance collateral in a member bank's warehouse for safekeeping, the Center and the member bank shall enter into a warehouse contract, the main points of which are as follows:

1. The warehouse shall, as far as possible, adopt the Center's opinions on the method of storing acceptance collateral.

2. The warehouse shall issue a goods report to the Center for the Center's acceptance collateral, whether at the time of entering the warehouse or when the warehouse originally kept it and the Center accepted it.

3. The Center may formulate report forms for acceptance collateral at any time and issue them to the warehouse, which shall fill them out in detail and submit them to the Center for filing.

4. The member bank acknowledges that the Center has the right to participate in the management of the part of the warehouse where acceptance collateral is stacked.

Article 20: The goods report of the member bank's warehouse shall record the following items and be signed by the warehouse supervisor:

1. Name of the collateral.

2. Quantity of the collateral.

3. Source of the collateral.

4. Packaging form.

5. Packaging mark.

6. Warehouse inspection status.

7. Other matters that should be noted.

Article 21: When the Center deposits acceptance collateral in a non-member bank's warehouse for safekeeping, it shall, to the extent possible, enter into a contract with each warehouse in accordance with the provisions of Article 19 of these detailed rules.

Article 22: The Center shall issue a list of collateral custody every month for the acceptance collateral received, stating the type and quantity of the collateral and the storage status, and submit it to the collateral management group of the Bank Note Acceptance Center Committee for review.

Article 23: The acceptance collateral received by the Center shall be inspected at any time by two or more members of the collateral management group of the Bank Note Acceptance Center Committee.

Accounting Categories

Chapter VI: Accounting

Article 24: The Center shall establish the following ledgers for registration when handling bank note acceptance matters:

1. Acceptance fund account.

2. Acceptance draft account.

3. Acceptance collateral account.

4. Acceptance collateral subsidiary ledger.

5. Acceptance receivables account.

6. Acceptance collateral disposal account.

7. Acceptance fee account.

8. Acceptance miscellaneous profit and loss account.

9. Acceptance expense account.

10. Date of receipts and payments account.

Chapter VII: Supplementary Provisions

Article 25: If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, they may be amended at any time.

Article 26: These detailed rules shall be resolved by the Bank Note Acceptance Center Committee of the Committee, approved by the Executive Committee of the Committee, and promulgated for implementation. The same shall apply to amendments.

"The Unofficial History of Chan Zhen" Published by Shanghai Magazine Company 148

Most of the famous novels of the Ming Dynasty, such as "Water Margin," "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," and "Jin Ping Mei Cihua," have printed editions. However, "The Unofficial History of Chan Zhen," compiled by Qingxi Daoren, has been rarely circulated. Although it is also a novel, the narratives are all based on historical facts. It is said that the events are well-founded and the language is organized. The rise and fall of the two dynasties are as clear as day, and the geographical map of the era is as brilliant as the stars. Focusing on Emperor Wu of Liang's belief in Buddhism and extending to Emperor Yang of Sui, the history is filled with poems, songs, jokes, and ridicule, thoroughly satirizing human nature and depicting the extremities of society. The work comprises 600,000 words, printed in two thick volumes, and is collated by Zhang Jinglu. It is listed as the 29th title in the "Rare Books of Chinese Literature" series. The popular edition is priced at only one yuan, and the special edition is one yuan and forty cents, which is nearly 80% cheaper than the original woodblock version. The book was released yesterday and is distributed by Shanghai Magazine Company.

Zhepigong Institute Established in Wusong 149

Sea jellyfish, also known as "zhepi," are produced in large quantities in the islands outside Wusongkou, such as Sijiao and Shengshan. They are transported by Ningbo fishing boats to Wusong, Shanghai, Suzhou, and other inland areas for sale. Wusong is the most important distribution center. Wang Pingcheng and Liu Jinshan, Ningbo merchants stationed in Wusong, have observed that the producers are sticking to the old ways and not focusing on improving the quality of the products, resulting in sluggish sales in various regions and inconsistent prices. Therefore, they have established the Zhepigong Institute at 97 Tongxing Road in Wusong to promote improvement and consolidation. The producers believe that the institute is highly beneficial to the production and interests of fishermen, so all cargo ships arriving in Wusong are required to report to the institute first.

Tang Mengwu Publishes Review Books on Civics for Senior and Junior High Schools 150

Tang Mengwu, a teacher at the Chinese Public School of the Shanghai Municipal Council, is a certified civics teacher for senior and junior high schools. During the winter vacation, based on his knowledge and experience and in accordance with the latest curriculum standards for senior and junior high schools issued by the Ministry of Education, he has compiled comprehensive review books on civics for both senior and junior high schools. The senior high school book is divided into subjects such as society, politics, law, economics, and ethics; the junior high school book is divided into subjects such as civics and morality, local autonomy, politics, law, and economics. Each book is organized into six sections. The selection of materials emphasizes practical application, and the ideas are intended to be orthodox. The books are formatted in a question-and-answer style, and the language is simple and easy to understand. The goal is to enable students in all grades of senior and junior high schools to engage in interesting reviews of civics subjects, both inside and outside the classroom, and to acquire basic knowledge. Therefore, the books are helpful for students in all grades of senior and junior high schools in preparing for holiday exams, entrance exams, and graduation exams. The books have been submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and to the Provincial Department of Education and the Municipal Bureau of Education for circulation among middle schools. The copyright belongs to the Pushi Xing Newspaper Agency in Junyi Lane, North Railway Station. The books are priced low, and they have already been reprinted within a month of their release.

Letter 157

To the Editor,

I am writing in regards to an article that you recently published in your local city news column. The article, titled "Hoodlums Gather at the Yihe Wharf in Hongkou to Gamble and Assault People," makes claims about a man named Shu Bin that are factually incorrect. The article claims, "A gambler named Wang Shubin operates a food shop at 220 Huaji Road. However, he enjoys gambling and goes to gamble every day. Yesterday, he suddenly had a dispute with a group of hoodlums over a trivial matter and suffered serious injuries." The facts of the case do not reflect what has been written in this article. I, Wang Shubin, operate the Dongmaoju Tianjin restaurant at 220 Huaji Road. Sailors frequently accumulate debt on their meals at my restaurant. Yesterday, I went to collect on these debts, and the debtors refused to pay. Instead, they ganged up and assaulted me. The claim that I, Shubin, am a gambler is false. It is merely hearsay. I am concerned that this will create a misunderstanding amongst the general public. Therefore, I request that you please correct the article as soon as possible.

Sincerely,

Wang Shubin

March 1, 25th year

After the Junior Cup, Youyou Wins the North China Daily News Cup. Defeated St. Francis 3-2 in Yesterday's Final. Youyou Led 2-0 in the First Half 159

After defeating Lancashire to win the Junior Cup last week, the Youyou B team defeated St. Francis 3-2 at the Shen Garden yesterday to win the North China Daily News Cup. Because both teams had evenly matched talent and many outstanding players, the game was very competitive and exciting. Youyou scored two goals in the first half, establishing a solid foundation. In the second half, St. Francis counterattacked strongly and also scored two goals, making the situation tense. Fortunately, Xu Wenkui's agility allowed Youyou to score a third goal, winning the game 3-2. These two teams were also the finalists for this cup last year, with St. Francis winning the championship. Each team has won one final in two years, which can be said to be a fair exchange.

Two Consecutive Goals

St. Francis has famous Portuguese players such as Foun Endeaye and So Sek, while Youyou has Xu Jiaokui, Xi Qiaosheng, Zhang Rong, etc. The central defender Lei Lianjin is a rare talent. Both sides were determined to win, and each did their best in offense and defense. However, St. Francis' coordination was not yet perfect, and Xu Wenkui, Xi Qiaosheng, and Luo Douwen repeatedly broke through their defense. Xu Wenkui opened the scoring, and Xi Qiaosheng added another goal. Although the St. Francis goalkeeper was good, he could not avoid a loss. Although Youyou's defense was alarmed several times, Zhu Qiu and others defended effectively, preserving their lead. Starting in the second half, Youyou continued to attack, and their momentum was still strong. However, St. Francis was unwilling to give in and tried to recover the lost goals. Foun, a young player who had been selected as a Shanghai Interport team member, was closely guarded by Yang Jinling and Zhang. The ball was shifted to the left and center. Portuguese star Endeaye broke into Youyou's goal area. Zhang Rong illegally tackled him in a dangerous situation, resulting in a penalty kick, which was kicked in by central defender Boer Tai. After losing the opportunity, St. Francis made a comeback. So Sek shot, and Foun rushed up to sweep the ball in. Wang Caigao rushed out to save the ball and fell to the ground. The ball fell to the side, and Wallach kicked it into the goal, tying the score at 2-2.

A Victory by a Narrow Margin

After that, the situation became even more intense. After Youyou kicked off from the center, they went straight to the enemy camp in one go. Ya Rent's ball handling mistake sparked a prairie fire. Then, Balo Ting made the same mistake. Xu Wenkui fought from east to west, got the ball, and shot, scoring the winning goal. Youyou then took the lead 3-2. St. Francis attacked several times, but Yan Lianjin defended the center with stability and experience. Even in several dangerous situations, Wang Caigao was able to turn the danger into safety. In front of the St. Francis goal, the Youyou forwards were seen darting in and out. The goalkeeper's technique was excellent, saving countless dangerous balls. When time ran out, Youyou avenged last year's defeat and won the North China Daily News Cup.

Points for Improvement in Guizhou Province's Education. The Ministry of Education Orders the Provincial Department of Education to Comply and Report. 167

The report on the inspection of education in Guizhou Province by Chen Lijiang, a commissioner of the Ministry of Education, has been reviewed and approved by the Ministry. On the 19th, the Ministry specifically listed the points for improvement in the province's education and ordered the Provincial Department of Education to comply and report. The points are listed as follows:

Regarding Primary Education: The primary schools in the province are mostly poorly equipped, the teaching methods are outdated, and the management is very lax. The Department of Education should urgently dispatch inspectors to conduct a general inspection of the counties and order the educational administrative organs in each county to formulate plans for establishing primary schools and promoting them year by year as the basis for improvement. Model primary schools should be established and gradually increased year by year. In the 25th year, at least one school should be established in Zunyi and Anshun counties. The Department of Education should hold a workshop for primary school teachers during the summer vacation of the 25th year and order each county to send primary school principals, teachers, and county government officials in charge of primary education administration to attend the workshop to improve the quality of primary school teachers.

2. Regarding Compulsory Education: The six short-term primary schools established in the provincial capital have too few students and should be enrolled as soon as possible. Moreover, how the school's performance affects short-term primary schools throughout the province is crucial and should be supervised at any time. The expenses of the short-term primary schools in the province this year are fully allocated monthly by the Department. However, the expenses for compulsory education should be raised by the local government as a principle. For the next fiscal year, each county should be ordered to follow the "Outline of Provisional Measures for Raising Funds for Compulsory Education in Provinces, Counties, and Cities" promulgated by the central government to find ways to raise funds to facilitate the process. The majority of short-term primary schools in the province are established independently, and the teachers are full-time, and their qualifications and academic abilities are generally still in line. They should also be ordered to concurrently run rural and village public education to promote it.

3. Regarding Secondary and Normal Education: No secondary school may hold classes on Sundays. This must be strictly enforced. The arrangement of courses in the school's teaching schedule must also be rationalized. Do not accommodate the convenience of part-time teachers by scheduling several hours of a certain subject consecutively in one morning or afternoon, causing students to feel tired and reducing teaching efficiency. Natural science courses should have experimental teachers who should personally guide students to do hands-on work and have experimental reports. Equipment should be expanded, and a unified procurement method should be developed. Secondary and normal school teachers are excessively part-time. The ratio of part-time to full-time teachers should be in accordance with the revised secondary school regulations. More full-time teachers should be hired. The principals of each school should prepare a list of qualified personnel in accordance with the regulations and submit it to the Department of Education for approval, and then the principals should hire them. Absenteeism and tardiness of teachers and students should be strictly prohibited. The method should be formulated by the Department of Education and submitted to the Ministry for implementation. The provincial secondary schools in the province should determine their establishment based on the source of their funding. If there are provincial secondary schools in the province that are funded by the county, they should be renamed county secondary schools or still be called provincial secondary schools, and the funding should be paid by the provincial treasury. Most of the secondary school buildings are too dilapidated and should have a complete renovation and construction plan, which should be practical and easy to implement. The school buildings that have been borrowed by the military should be recovered for use as soon as possible. Students in secondary schools in the provincial capital often wander outside at night. Each secondary school should be strictly managed, and students must live on campus. If there are still cases of students being allowed to be undisciplined, the principal should be responsible. There are too few normal schools in the province and normal school districts should be designated and added year by year, with the goal of one school per district. County secondary schools should also be appropriately converted into simplified normal schools and rural normal schools or affiliated rural normal classes to train compulsory education teachers. The affiliated primary schools of the existing Guizhou Normal School and the Women's Normal School have very little contact with the normal school headquarters. The existing internship methods should be improved so that students can participate in the administrative management and teaching of the affiliated primary school in various ways for training.

4. Regarding Vocational Education: The proportion of vocational education funding should be in accordance with the ratio set by the Ministry, and a detailed plan for the future development of vocational education should be formulated based on the economic construction of the province. The Department of Education should consider the actual situation and order each county's secondary schools to be converted into junior vocational schools. The provincial junior vocational school is well-managed, but more internships should be provided, and cooperation with construction agencies should be established to achieve practical results.

You are expected to improve in accordance with the above points and promptly submit a report on the handling situation for future reference. This order.

Public Concession Chinese School Subsidies Increased and Approved. Concession Education Funding Reaches Maximum Limit 171

The Information Office of the Public Concession stated that foreign and Chinese private schools in the Public Concession apply to the Bureau of Public Works for subsidies each year in accordance with regulations. For this year's subsidy, the Foreign School Affairs Committee organized a subsidy review committee to make recommendations, stipulating a total of 169,000 yuan, of which schools run by the Japanese accounted for 128,000 yuan. Subsequently, the Japanese Residents Group in Shanghai petitioned for an additional subsidy of 66,000 yuan. This proposal was submitted to the Board of Directors by the School Affairs Committee for review. Later, the Finance Committee convened a meeting on the 17th of this month to discuss the results of the decision to recommend to the Board of Directors an additional 11,000 yuan in addition to the originally set 128,000 yuan (the same as last year). The Board of Directors, at its regular meeting on Sunday, approved the Finance Committee's recommendation to increase the subsidy to Japanese children's schools by 11,000 yuan.

As for Chinese private schools, the subsidies they should receive this year were also advocated by the Chinese School Subsidy Review Committee, from 200,876 yuan last year to 247,850 yuan, because 37 new Chinese children's schools were established by private individuals this year, with a total of 8,350 students, an increase of more than 23%. A corresponding economic subsidy is also proposed. Later, the Director of the Finance Department only agreed to consolidate the amount from last year's 200,800 yuan to an even 210,000 yuan, on the grounds that the financial situation this year is tight and all aspects need to be tightened. Fortunately, all departments of the Bureau of Public Works can appreciate this intention and have seen considerable results. However, the expenses of the Education Department in 1936 have increased compared to last year, because in addition to the subsidy, the internal expenses of this year have increased by 51,000 yuan compared to last year. The School Affairs Committee said that the application for subsidies for the 37 new Chinese schools has been deemed satisfactory, and the original amount of 247,000 yuan of the Review Committee should not be rejected again. After a discussion by the Finance Committee on the 17th of this month, with the consent of the Director of the Finance Department, it was agreed that an additional 19,000 yuan should be added on top of last year's subsidy limit, bringing the total to 227,160 yuan. A member of the Accounts Committee then reminded that the public concession education funding had previously been stipulated not to exceed 2% of the total donation and land price tax. Now the concession education funding, excluding the currently proposed increase of 11,000 yuan for Japanese children's schools and 19,000 yuan for Chinese school subsidies, has reached 1.84% of the total donation and property tax. If the proposed increase is added, it may reach 1.9%. After discussions among the members, it was agreed that the 1936 subsidy for Chinese private schools should be increased by 19,000 yuan, bringing the total to 227,760 yuan.

When the Board of Directors of the Bureau of Public Works discussed this matter on Wednesday, a member of the Board proposed that what should be made known is that the current concession education funding has reached the previously stipulated maximum amount (i.e., 2% of the total donation and land price tax). Therefore, all private schools in the future must not gradually increase due to the issuance of subsidies by the authorities. It must be known that those who receive financial assistance due to requests in the future must be allocated from the existing subsidies already received by each school. Therefore, the Chairman of the Board of Directors further suggested that the existing regulations should be reaffirmed now, that is, the public concession education funding, including all subsidies, must not exceed 2% of the total donation and land price tax. The above-mentioned increase in the number of subsidies was then passed.

Mr. Ye Yuhu and Mr. Wu Zhihui's Letters to the Wu-Yue History and Geography Research Association (2) 173

— Zhang Feng

Old Mr. Wu Zhihui was a party friend who negotiated several times in Shanghai during the early years of the Republic. Since the 25th year, his teaching career has been a floating and sinking one. He eats at the east house and sleeps at the west house, and finally neither the east head nor the west head is attached. Who is more esteemed than the one who leisurely spends his years and soars in the central hub? Before and after the meeting, if I could let him know about this matter, he would not laugh and say that the world is in trouble, old friends are separated, and he knows that. He has a little friend who can recite Egyptian and Babylonian characters, but he cannot hear the stories of his hometown. I, Feng, do not pity myself, but Old Mr. Wu may think it is a pity. He will come to the school and visit the thatched cottage. At that time, I, Feng, will have a short untitled poem to discuss. The poem says, "The little gray grandson crawls on the ground in his clothes, begs the official to find ancient relics, and the principal catches the errand boy." Old Mr. Wu's humor is famous throughout the world. He can smile and ponder together, which is enough to bring joy for a moment and eliminate sorrow for all eternity. I will write again in a few days. March 10th, the 25th year, Zhang Feng respectfully bows. A summary of the investigation of ancient relics is attached.

Attached is a report and summary of Zhang Feng's personal investigation of the history and geography of Wu-Yue in the past two years. In each investigation, there are many disappointments. Occasionally, I see one or two relics that are not related to the address, which are not included. The "discoveries" mentioned in this article are the initial findings, and the "identifications" are confirmed afterwards.

1. Tongxu, April 10th, 24th year, Wu Qiming and Zhang Feng, discovered a Jin tomb. The Diaoyu Terrace of Ziling is not a huge stone building. 2. Yan City, May 12th to 15th, Jiang Shangyu, Chu Shaotang, Chen Songmao, Jiang Dayi, Guo Weiping, Zhang Feng, discovered the ruins, with pottery shards, iron slag, red clay pottery balls, decayed wood, etc. Two decisions were made after several days of investigation. 3. Chagang, same as above, 14th day, same as above, identified bronze weights and pottery such as Zunlei Fanghu. On the same day, identified Han and Jin tomb bricks. 4. Lujiabang, June 5th, Jiang Dayi, Chen Songmao, Zhang Feng, identified three pottery Zun. 5. Kunshan, same time and date, same personnel, discovered Han bricks and pottery shards. 6. Shuangqiao, July 24th, Zong Songqing, Wu Heming, Zhang Feng, discovered stone tools, identified wall supplies, small Wang Jian, Han wells, Han bricks, pottery jugs, etc. 7. Jinshan, August 14th, Chen Yuncen, Huang Zhongchang, Zhang Feng, identified pottery shards and Han well ruins, discovered copper shards, Maoshi tools, red clay iron slag pottery jugs, etc. There were a total of six visits before and after, and one visit was spent staying in an oil truck. According to the Jinshan ruins, the first discovery was an ancient well, which was mistakenly regarded as a defense against Japanese pirates at the time. Huang Bohui and his brothers paid attention to the pottery shards for the second time. This trip was the third visit. 8. Zhapu, October 11th, Xu Genwu, Cao Jun, Zhang Feng, discovered the ancient Haijian City, which was moved three times after the second year of Yongjian during the reign of Emperor Shun of the Han Dynasty, and investigated the old Donggong Road. 9. Shangxi Temple, December, Zhang Renfu and Zhang Feng obtained five stone oxen. A former monk from Suzhou, Jiang Dayi, Cao Jian, and Zhang Feng identified pottery shards and red clay from the ruins of the old city and unearthed a beast tripod foot. This city was discovered by Jiang Cao and the other two gentlemen in previous investigations. 11. Wu Old City, January 8th, Wang Peizheng, Cao Jian, Jiang Dayi, Zhang Feng, inspected the Gaogang and the ruins of the abandoned base. 12. Zhang Shicheng City, February 18th, Jiang Dayi, Zhang Feng, the city is well preserved, and the old records are missing. According to Zhu Yizun's poetry, the new records are confirmed. 13. Jianchi Qianren Stone, same as above, same as above, checked as an ancient quarry. The inclination and angle of the Qianren Stone layers are consistent. Wu Wang's tomb should have been destroyed. The bamboo slips that flowed out in the Song Dynasty and the exposed tomb gate at the end of the Ming Dynasty should still be preserved and待查. 14. Gu Wu Cultural Layer, February 19th, Zhang Ziyi, Jiang Daqi, Zhang Feng drew a detailed map of a cultural layer in a pit more than three meters deep and gave it to Mr. Jiang for continued work. On the same day, I saw one of the old ten pottery pots unearthed in the old house, and two pottery pots unearthed a year earlier in Lengtan. 15. Three people holding a stone umbrella, January 20th, Jiang Dayi, Zhang Feng, climbed to the top of Tianping and confirmed that it was not an ancient relic, but a rocky road. Pottery shards have been seen, and the ruins of Guanwa can be explored. Another plan is being prepared and given to Jiang Cao and the other two gentlemen to continue the investigation. 16. Yuepu Seawall, February 13th, Zhang Shan, Zhang Feng, Jiang Dayi checked the objects of a certain country that had sunk, but did not get them, waiting for further investigation. 17. Doumen, planned to be investigated during the spring break. 18. The junction of Zhejiang and Fujian, planned to be investigated during the summer vacation. 19. Zhuji Xiaoshan, planned to live there for more than a month during the summer vacation to investigate. 20. Hypothetical shell mound, the address has been obtained, and it is indeed a shell mound. Objects must be accompanied by evidence to prove it, and one visit will be made to investigate. 21. Taibo City, etc. Taibo City is not necessarily in Wuxi, Qi Nu's tomb may not be a relic, and the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway broke through an ancient city. Zhengyi has a relic, all of which are planned to be confirmed as soon as possible. 22. Jiaocheng, is being designed for investigation. 23. The First Emperor's Post Road, the post road spans two provinces and passes through six or seven counties. It is discontinuous and incomplete, making it difficult to investigate. Even though it is near my hometown, there is no suitable method. 24. Hudu Fortress, this was noticed in 24 years, and has been investigated many times without success. (Note) Archaeological investigation is difficult and tedious, and learning has a teacher's method. The matter belongs to a specialty. It is difficult to say who started the picture. Authors in various countries attach importance to the time and date and the first discoverer as morality. I hope that writers, journalists, and propagandists will pay attention to the time and date of discovery and the names of the discoverers. The place names and purposes in the article are temporarily kept secret, please understand.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (2) (0) (7) 174

— Original by Lluisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"No, I think that little child you just mentioned, the elegant woman he married, was far more of a creator than the wild Nanen he met in his youth; or even more, the wise and virtuous mother-like woman often secretly protected him, like Little Mei protecting Little Qiao, was the most important to his success." Mrs. Shu, when speaking, looked back at her mother, who was sitting near Meg, and looked full of the gentle and virtuous dignity of old age. Mr. Lau gave her a filial glance and replied in a very sincere manner:

"All three of them were very helpful to him. Now I can understand that these girls must be very helpful to your children."

"But not more than the children helped them; it's mutual, I tell you. Ned helped Little Mei a lot with his music; Don manages Nanen better than any of us; Little Qiao teaches your golden curl children, effortlessly and with very satisfactory results, and Flitz even calls them Arzt and Junker. (Note 12) Ah! What a pity! If the men and women in the world could trust, understand, and help each other like my children, what a good place this world would be!" Mrs. Shu said, with a kind of trance in her eyes, as if she was seeing a wonderful new society, in which the people lived happily and innocently together, like a group of children in Mei Manor.

(Note 12) Arzt Rogev Achan 1515-1568 was a famous British scholar and educator. His work Sohoolmaoter praised the accomplishments of his female disciple Jane Grey (Lady Jane Grey, 1573-1545).

After the Implementation of the New Subsidiary Currency 178

Since the promulgation and implementation of the Subsidiary Currency Ordinance on January 11, the Ministry of Finance has been engaged in minting. The prototype coins were submitted to the government and the Executive Yuan for record on February 5. On February 6, Proclamation No. 134 stipulated the issuance on February 10. Initially, the currency was not often seen on the market, but recently it has been seen in stores for change. However, it is still not enough to meet demand, and counterfeits have been discovered, causing users to be wary. Recently, several cases have been cracked, which should reduce such activity. As of the end of February, 890,000 nickel 20-fen coins had been minted (legal tender 178,000 yuan), 2,700,000 nickel 10-fen coins (legal tender 270,000 yuan), 4,680,000 nickel 5-fen coins (legal tender 234,000 yuan), 25,500,000 copper 1-fen coins (legal tender 255,000 yuan), and 8,520,000 copper half-fen coins (legal tender 42,600 yuan). Production has continued in March, and the coins have been distributed to various places for circulation.

Pingshui green tea from Zhejiang Province has long relied on the United States as its primary market. Shen Bao Children's Special

Shen Bao Children's Essay Contest

What Kind of Person I Want to Be in the Future 196

— Xiong Peizhu, Jiangdu County Dongcheng Elementary School

I am an elementary school student. My living environment consists of a beautiful school and a kind family. My companions are mostly children, who spend their days playing and laughing. We have never thought about our future. On the National Day of the 24th year, the principal said, "Children! You are still young and only know how to play all day. This is certainly a lively and innocent behavior. Not just you, all the children in the world are like this. But you must remember that our motherland is not the strong England or the wealthy America. Our motherland is a weak and endangered China. Therefore, your responsibility is very great. Remember! The revival of China depends on you children!..." I was moved by these words. Alas! "Our motherland is a weak and endangered country." How should I strive? What kind of person should I emulate in the future? Undoubtedly, I am willing to dedicate my life to working hard and fighting for our motherland, driving away our enemies, developing our country, and reviving our nation, becoming a patriot who sacrifices for the country.

Newton's Childhood 197

— Junming

Newton was born on December 25, 1642. He was a scientist. In 1667, he invented the prism. He also invented the reflecting telescope. He died in 1727 at the age of eighty-five. His childhood was very interesting.

Because he lost his parents at a young age, he lived with his uncle. Although he was an orphan, he approached everything with the attitude of "Why is it like this? What exactly is it like that?" This had a great influence on his later inventions.

One day, he was taking a walk alone in the garden and saw an apple falling from an apple tree to the ground. You might think this is a small and ordinary thing, nothing strange. However, this young scientist Newton, strangely enough, refused to let it go easily. He thought to himself, "Why doesn't the apple fall upwards or sideways? Why does it fall vertically?" Finally, he discovered what is known as the "law of gravity," which attracts all things. Children! You must pay attention. Scientific inventors discover principles from very ordinary things that others do not notice. It lies in paying attention to everything.

Another anecdote: one morning, he was in the midst of his research when a servant brought eggs and a pot to cook breakfast. Newton said, "Just put the eggs and the pot here. I'll cook them myself." Later, he went to cook them himself. After waiting for tens of minutes, the water in the pot was boiling. He thought the eggs were cooked, but when he opened it, it wasn't eggs, but a watch rolling in the boiling water. Imagine how focused he was! Truly, he was single-minded!

We Are All Young Soldiers 198

— Tiewu

Elementary school students, young in age,

Diligent in studies, conscientious in work,

Lively and innocent,

We are the sons of China,

We are all young soldiers.

We have learned geography,

We know which mountains, rivers, and towns there are;

We have studied history,

We understand how a nation can survive;

We often do manual labor,

Forging iron bones and copper muscles;

How to defend against poison gas? How to charge? It's all in the books;

How to save the country? How to save oneself? The books also show us good directions;

We will be able to fight in the future,

We will also be able to teach others,

We are the sons of China,

We are all young soldiers.

Sky Hotel 199

— Shayou

—Although we don't have it yet, we should still know—

The Zeppelin factory in Germany recently built a large airship, preparing to fly regularly across the Atlantic. The equipment of that airship is simply like an "air hotel."

This airship is divided into two levels. The lower level contains twenty-five rooms and can carry fifty passengers. Each room has two berths, hot and cold running water pipes, a wardrobe for hanging clothes, and a writing desk. In addition, there is a dining hall with a capacity of thirty guests. The upper level is a smoking room, a bathroom, a washroom, a kitchen, a crew rest room, and a storage room.

This airship will start scheduled flights this spring, with each voyage taking two days and the fare being four hundred gold dollars per passenger.

With the aviation industry developing so rapidly, and with such comfortable and convenient travel, I'm afraid that in less than fifty years, ships and trains will be relegated to specialized cargo transport, while passenger travel will be entirely carried out by airships or airplanes.

Children! Backward nations are retreating to the mountains and forests, living the primitive life of the Wu Huai and Ge Tian clans; civilized nations are rising from the land and sea, riding clouds and mist, and living the life of immortals in the sky. We are now being forced to go into the mountains or hell. How can we not strive and advance?

What a great Berlin airship!

What a great Berlin airship! 200

Owl 201

— Zhang Yian

Because of its appearance and nature, the owl is disliked and regarded as a symbol of danger; in the West, the owl is known as a philosopher and conspirator. Indeed, its appearance is indeed different from ordinary birds: a large head, large eyes, a small face, a sharp hooked beak, and two tufts of hair on its head, resembling a pair of ears (but those are not ears). The upper half of its head, from the hairline to the eyes, does look a bit like a cat's head. We call it a "cat-headed owl," which is a pictorial name. In the dictionary, its original name is "xiao" (owl). (Figure A)

Its only special characteristic is that it sleeps during the day and comes out at night, preying on small birds and other animals in the dark. Sometimes, in the still of the night, we hear a "ju li ju li" sound flying past in the air. Many timid people mistake it for a ghost's cry, but it is actually the old gentleman owl on patrol. It takes advantage of the fact that small animals are sound asleep to suddenly attack and hunt them to feed its belly.

You might ask: How can it see in the dark? That is why it has a pair of large eyes. It can not only see, but also see things from high up and far away that we cannot see. Although its eyes have similarities with cat eyes, there are also differences. The similarity is that both can see things in very dark places, and their pupils can enlarge or shrink very flexibly. The difference is that when a cat's pupil shrinks, it goes from a vertical olive shape to a very thin vertical line (Figure C—), while an owl's pupil remains round when it shrinks (Figure C). When it looks at dark places, its pupil enlarges greatly, almost the size of the entire eyeball (Figure B). However, when it encounters strong light, it shrinks smaller than a match head. The structure and function of its pupil are the same as the aperture of a camera lens: when the camera lens needs to take pictures in a dark place, the aperture must be enlarged; when taking pictures of brightly lit scenes, the aperture must be reduced. This is how the amount of light received is adjusted. The pupil function of cats and owls works exactly the same way. Human pupils also have the same function, but their efficiency and flexibility are far inferior to theirs.

In addition to small birds, owls also eat mice and even snails. Its feathers are different from other birds in that they are light and soft, so it doesn't make flapping sounds when it flies. Moreover, its structure is special and won't make noise when the wind blows. Otherwise, the small animals it wants to catch will hear it and hide.

The Shanghai Zhao Feng Park Zoo recently has a live owl in a corner of the bird house. If children have the opportunity, they can go and observe it and compare it with what is described in this article.

Additional Tourist Destination

Guangzhou 202

— Zhou Qifeng

When we travel to major cities like Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and Qingdao, what we see is wide and flat roads, neat and sturdy buildings, and bustling traffic. Everything tries its best to express the civilization of modern material. But these are all achievements managed by foreigners in the concessions. Once outside the concessions, there is a sense of inferiority, which makes you wonder if it is another world. Only Guangzhou is a prosperous city built entirely by the power of the Chinese people. The density of population, the prosperity of industry and commerce, and the perfection of municipal facilities are no less than those of Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou and other places. If we don't think it is glorious to rely on foreigners, then the number one city in China should be given to Guangzhou.

However, the prosperity and glory of Guangzhou is not only due to human efforts. Natural forces and the geographical environment are also enough to make Guangzhou prosperous. Guangzhou is located in the delta of the Pearl River, a very fertile alluvial plain. It is also located at the estuary of the West, North, and East Rivers, and is the starting point of the Yuehan, Guangjiu, and Chegguang three railways. If there were no obstacles from Hong Kong, the future of Guangzhou would be truly limitless.

Guangzhou is the birthplace of the revolution. The Tomb of the Seventy-Two Martyrs of Huanghuagang and the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall stand majestic and inspire awe. Remembering the firm and outstanding fighting spirit of the martyrs, and looking at the current national situation, one cannot help but feel emotional!

Map of Guangzhou and Vicinity 203

Ten Minutes of Science Teaching 204

— Baitao

The things surrounding us are truly mysterious! Machines working in place of people; generators producing electricity; trains speeding; airplanes flying; radio transmitting sound and images; miners extracting gold, silver, copper, iron, tin, coal, etc. from mines; printers printing thousands of books, newspapers, and various colored drawings. Looking again at the fields, we see that grains can grow and bear fruit; a single seed can grow into a large tree; various insects are born and die; and there are fish, birds, flowers, and plants; the sky rains and thunders; the sun, moon, and stars move; and the four seasons change continuously. Truly, there is nothing that is not strange, and there is no end to what can be said. All these mysterious things surrounding us have an attraction, attracting us to study them. Because they are mysterious and interesting, many scientists are moved by curiosity and pursue them year after year.

It is not difficult to understand these mysterious things. We only need to put in the effort to study them. Here, I will continue to write about these mysterious scientific knowledge in a systematic way, paying special attention to small experiments. After you have done these experiments, you will slowly step into the door of science.

The First Mysterious Thing

Many things are not always the same as their appearance; when we see them and find them strange, we should examine them carefully. For example, we cannot turn a piece of iron into something else. But if you immerse a shiny knife or a bright iron piece in a certain blue liquid, take it out and see that it has suddenly turned into copper. How strange is that! Originally, that blue liquid is copper sulfate dissolved in water, and copper sulfate is made by dissolving copper in sulfuric acid. So, that blue liquid contains copper. Strange! The steel knife has turned into copper! Is that really the case? But you can't see it. When you immerse the iron, some copper precipitates on it, so when you take it out, a layer of shiny copper is plated on the iron surface, as if it has turned into copper. In the past, people plated silver objects with a layer of gold and said that the object was gold. In practice, a piece of silver is immersed in an acid, the silver is dissolved, and then a layer of gold is plated on it. This tells us a simple rule, that is, one metal cannot be turned into another metal.

Many things surrounding us prevent us from seeing their true colors; just like in blue copper sulfate, we cannot see the copper. For example, children in the city often see people using gas to light lamps or cook. This kind of gas lamp conceals coal. You can do a small experiment: if you put some coal in a large pipe (such as the long pipe used by rural people to smoke moist tobacco), and put the pipe on an alcohol lamp or stove to heat. If you cover the top of the pipe tightly and only let the air out of the tube, gas will be released from the coal immediately, and it will start to flow out from the top of the tube. Strike a match and you can burn the gas. Where does this gas come from, and why is it flammable? Originally, strange! The smoke at the top of the pipe is burning! The gas conceals flammable coal. Another strange thing is the black, gelatinous substance left in the pipe, which we call coal tar, and can also be made into beautiful dyes.

The lead used to make airplanes, airships, and other things is hidden in ordinary soil! Many things in the world are not always the same as their appearance, which is very mysterious. (This article has three illustrations, which will be published in the next issue.)

Friendship 205

— Yan Chonglou

There are no boundaries between children, so children are all friends who don't need introductions.

Within the family: brothers and sisters are the closest friends, not only because they spend a lot of time together, but also because of the bond of siblings.

Within the school: male and female classmates study together, exercise and play together, which is a mutual aid friendship.

Within the society: poor and wealthy children love each other, and there is no discrimination, which can be said to be an equal friendship.

Within the world: regardless of black, white, yellow, or red races, adults may be calculating the boundaries of races and creating racial wars, but children only know the friendship of the same year and do not know the differences of races; this can be said to be a natural friendship.

There is no money or power between children... these things hinder true friendship or create false friendship, so children's friendship is the purest and greatest.

Children's Corner

Don't Be Discouraged 206

— Wen Ying, a third-grade female student at Wanzhu Elementary School

I am a twelve-year-old elementary school student. When I was seven years old, my mother sent me to a rural school to study. At that time, I only read books like "People, hands, bamboo, knives, rulers" and "Older brother, younger brother, younger sister". After studying for about two years, in May of the year I was nine years old, my family moved to Shanghai to live, and spent a summer vacation.

At the beginning of July, when the schools recruited students for the autumn semester, my father registered me at Wanzhu Elementary School. The next day, he took me to the school to take the entrance exam. At that time, I had just arrived in Shanghai and was very timid. In addition, the schools in Shanghai were very different from those in the countryside. There were many students in the Shanghai schools. When I took the entrance exam, I was so scared that I almost died. As a result, I was not accepted.

At this time, I had no choice but to stay at home and not study. I thought that studying in Shanghai was really not easy, so I might as well go back to the countryside to study. When I was feeling discouraged, Bing Ge, the landlord downstairs, came upstairs and saw that I looked unhappy. He asked me why I was unhappy, and I told him about not passing the entrance exam. Bing Ge quickly said to me, "In our era of children's drawings, no matter what we do! If we don't succeed, we shouldn't be discouraged, but should strive to improve." He also said, "Failure is the mother of success. We must not be discouraged if we fail in one step." After listening to Bing Ge's advice, I reviewed my old books at home for the past six months. When I encountered words or sentences that I didn't know or couldn't explain, I asked my father. In this way, when I was ten years old, I took the entrance exam again in the spring and passed. I was very happy in my heart. Recalling Bing Ge's words, they were really correct. We children should not be discouraged. I have been studying until this year and have been promoted to the A group of the intermediate group. Now I am writing down my own experience, hoping that children all over the country, no matter what they do, if they encounter failure, they must strive and fight, "Don't be discouraged" is the key.

Biography of a Righteous Dog (12) 207

— Xinqing

Little Aloys was indeed one of the richest children in the village. She had neither brothers nor sisters; her blue velvet dress never had holes in it. When she first participated in Holy Communion, she wore a gorgeous Mechlin lace bonnet on her soft hair, which her grandmother and mother had worn when they were young. Although she was only twelve years old, half of the men in the village already paid attention to her, thinking that she would be a good wife for their sons in the future. But little Aloys was a naive and innocent girl who didn't know her own background. The little friend she loved the most and often played with was little Nanlos and his dog.

Her father, Mr. Coghans, was also a very kind man, but he was a bit too serious. One day, he went to the meadow behind the kitchen and ran into the three of them together.

His little daughter Aloys was sitting in the middle of a pile of hay, and Birdy's tan head was resting on her body. They were surrounded by wreaths of poppies and blue cornflowers; and the child Nanlos was taking a burnt branch and drawing them both on a smooth pine board as realistically as possible.

The miller looked at the portrait, and tears unconsciously welled up in his eyes, because the face in the portrait looked very similar to little Aloys, and he loved his daughter very much. Immediately, he reprimanded little Aloys and pretended that her mother was calling her. Little Aloys was very scared and ran into the house crying. Mr. Coghans turned around, took the pine board from little Nanlos's hand, and said with a trembling body, "Why are you doing such a mindless thing?" Little Nanlos blushed, lowered his head, and replied softly, "I like to draw whatever I see."

Mr. Coghans was silent for a while, then took a franc in his hand, stretched it out, and said to little Nanlos, "I said this is a mindless thing, a waste of time; but you draw little Aloys so vividly that her mother will definitely like it. Take this silver coin and give me this painting."

The blush on little Nanlos's face faded away. He raised his head, put his hands behind his back, and said quietly, "Mr. Coghans, please keep the money and the painting. You want to treat me very well." Then he called Birdy over, and together they crossed the field and went home. As he walked, he murmured to Birdy, "Although he gave me the franc, I must not accept it, because I am unwilling to sell her portrait."
