Shen Bao Local Supplement - Amateur Weekly

Current Affairs Research

Germany's Advance into the Rhineland and the European Situation 208

— Zhong Zhen

The result of World War I's sacrifice of countless lives and property was the Treaty of Versailles, a contract of servitude for the German people. Through Germany's relentless struggles over more than a decade, this treaty has been gradually torn apart. Initially, reparations were reduced to complete cessation of payments. Subsequently, with Hitler's rise to power, he unilaterally declared rearmament. The Saar region was reclaimed through a plebiscite. Most recently, troops were directly sent to occupy the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland, thoroughly destroying the Treaty of Versailles. Most of the Treaty of Versailles has been torn up. Under the circumstances of Germany's free action on its territory and denial of its obligations, it can be said to be completely equivalent to waste paper. At present, the only shackles imposed on Germany by the Treaty of Versailles that have not yet been removed are the former territories in Eastern Europe ceded to Poland and other countries that have not been restored, and the overseas colonies ceded and transferred to the victorious nations that have not been recovered. However, all these are no longer a question of whether Germany will continue to abide by the treaty obligations of the Treaty of Versailles, but only a question of whether its actual power can fulfill its aspirations. In fact, there is no need to talk about the binding force of international treaties.

The demilitarized zone of the Rhineland was stipulated in the Treaty of Versailles, which stated that "Germany shall not maintain or construct any fortifications" and "shall not station any troops in this area, nor prepare for mobilization in this area." After the signing of the Treaty of Versailles, countries such as Britain and France stationed troops here in order to monitor and force Germany to fulfill the treaty and extract reparations. Later, the withdrawal of British and French troops from the Rhineland was not because they felt Germany could not bear this oppression, which caused social poverty and unrest, and there was a great possibility of this triggering a revolution. Therefore, these two imperialist countries allowed the reduction of reparations and the withdrawal of troops from the Rhineland. Of course, there was also the role of Britain already intending to gradually restore German power to prevent France from becoming too powerful and Russia from advancing westward. But at this time, the so-called Locarno Treaty was also established, in which Germany's obligations in the Rhineland region were reiterated, and another iron chain was tied to Germany. It was also stipulated that if Germany violated the Treaty of Versailles and the Locarno Treaty, all countries should take joint action to assist each other. The so-called mutual assistance was, in fact, mainly to prevent Germany from restoring its armed forces in the Rhineland area and 　　 France, in order to guarantee France's security.

But what about now? Since Germany automatically announced its rearmament and thus had considerable strength, it completely mobilized a large army and marched into the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland on the 7th and 8th of this month without adopting a negotiating attitude. According to the existing number of German troops, there are already 60,000 troops in the area. The soaring of German planes, the installation of artillery and anti-aircraft guns, and the reconstruction of artillery emplacements along the borders of neighboring France, Belgium, and the Netherlands, etc., are gradually intensifying the implementation of its own plans, regardless of any protests or criticisms. Because of this, France is also actively deploying troops and busily strengthening its border defenses. Moreover, Germany is taking a threatening posture in the unfolding of this tense situation, indicating that if anyone wants to enforce treaty rights to interfere with its free actions, it will not hesitate to resort to bloody warfare. Therefore, the attention of the whole world has once again focused on this event. Everyone recognizes that it is bigger and more tense than the storms stirred up between European imperialist countries by the Italo-Ethiopian War, and there is a great sense that war is imminent. Because no matter how serious the Italo-Ethiopian War is, it is still limited to the struggle for colonies in Africa, while Germany's rearmament of the Rhineland is an expansion of direct conflict within European imperialism, igniting the fuse for the explosion of the powder keg on the European continent.

Judging from Germany's rearmament in the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland this time, although it seems superficially tense, it may not immediately lead to war. Even the final outcome of this event may very well lead to the shifting of the tense atmosphere in Western Europe to Eastern Europe in the future. Because Hitler's dispatch of troops into the Rhineland area and the declaration of not complying with the obligations of the Locarno Treaty are under the pretext of opposing the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. He believes that the Franco-Soviet Pact is a military alliance and hostile act of encirclement against Germany, and therefore Germany has no obligation to abide by the Locarno Pact. Of course, this claim by Germany is just an excuse, a smokescreen. Its true intention is to complete its absolute freedom to restore its military deployment within the former German territory under this pretext, and to abolish any treaty constraints imposed on it by the victorious countries. Because, in fact, the essence of the Franco-Soviet Pact can only be said to be defensive rather than offensive for both France and the Soviet Union. Neither France nor the Soviet Union has any territorial ambitions or possibility of aggression against Germany. Therefore, as long as Germany does not further threaten France and the Soviet Union, and France and the Soviet Union jointly take any military action against Germany 　 make sure there is absolutely no 　 actual situation. Germany is not unaware of this. However, Germany knows this, but still uses the Franco-Soviet Pact as an excuse, directly sending troops into the Rhineland regardless of treaties. There is a deep meaning in this.

When we analyze Germany's actions, we should understand that the reason is not limited to restoring the armament on the Rhine, but also to weaken the constraints and pressure imposed on its Eastern European policy by the Franco-Soviet Pact. The fact is very clear. Everyone knows that the existing state of absolute opposition between France and Germany makes it impossible for them to think of any territorial ambitions towards each other. Therefore, in Western Europe, Germany's ambition is at most to demand the restoration of the Rhineland's state of military readiness, so that it becomes Germany's completely sovereign and free territory. However, France is reluctant to grant even this small favor, which has created irreconcilable contradictions between the two countries. In Germany, because the recovery of overseas colonies and the lost territories ceded to Poland and other countries are the objects of imperialist development, it is bound to choose Russia. However, France, fearing Germany's rise, restricts its development with the Franco-Soviet Pact. This makes Germany deeply grieved and unable to avoid resolutely eliminating the root of the contradiction in Western Europe in order to facilitate its Eastern European policy. Therefore, on the one hand, it resolutely completes the necessary desire for its imperialist survival, cancels the constraints imposed on it in the Rhineland area by the treaty, and on the other hand, it attempts to reduce the conflicting factors of the incessant disputes between France and Germany, so as to further establish a relative coordination with France and achieve the effect of undermining the Franco-Soviet Pact. We only need to look at Germany's proposal to conclude a non-aggression treaty between various capitalist countries immediately after the restoration of armament in the Rhineland, including Britain, France, Belgium, Italy, Poland, etc., but excluding Russia, and the proposal to revise the Locarno Treaty and the Western European Air Pact, in order to remove France's unease and suspicion, etc., to understand.

Of course, France is still unwilling to accept Germany's demands because of the fear of the future dangers of Germany's rise. Therefore, the issue of Germany's rearmament in the Rhineland has immediately caused a serious situation between Germany and France. But in fact, France will eventually succumb, and even be forced to coordinate with Germany to reduce its burden on the Franco-Soviet Pact. Because Germany not only threatens it with war, making it dare not refuse to yield without the assistance of Britain and Italy; but also because of the contradictions between Britain and Italy, even if Britain is afraid that Germany will come out to support Italy, it has to hold Germany back. Also, because Britain has always been willing to prop up Germany to prevent Russia, it must buy off Germany. Therefore, Britain has always secretly supported Germany's proposal for a Western European Air Pact, wanting to remove the opposition between France and Germany in Western Europe. Therefore, Britain this time will not only not actively oppose Germany's breach of contract in rearming the Rhineland, but even mediate, exerting pressure on France to gradually accept Germany's proposals for the revision of the Locarno Pact, the creation of the Western European Air Pact, and the establishment of a non-aggression treaty. As for Italy, it is now most concerned about the scramble for African colonies. It can only take advantage of the tense atmosphere of the Rhineland issue to coerce for its own interests, and it will not benefit France's position. This has been proven by its current expression of indifference and neutrality. Thus　France will be isolated and helpless on the Rhineland issue, and will not dare to independently use force to punish Germany's breach of contract, and will eventually only gradually soften, compromise, and succumb. If the development of this fact reaches the realization of Germany's proposal, that is, it is realized under the mediation and support of Britain, and even pressure on France, then the tense atmosphere caused by the restoration of the Rhineland, if it does not accidentally trigger a war here, will be transferred to Eastern Europe. This is the possible future of its development.

Outlying Postal Agency

Maqun Sports Meet 209

— Ermike Tu

Suiyuan Baotou Correspondence

Suiyuan is a sparsely populated place. Its area is the largest among the current so-called five provinces of North China, but the population distribution averages only two people per square mile. The land is very barren, and compared with the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in the interior, it can simply be called a barren land. Therefore, it has never attracted people's attention. Since the fall of the four northeastern provinces and the issue of Inner Mongolia's autonomy centered on Baiyemiao, this line has aroused deep attention from the Chinese people. Recently, due to political, military, and diplomatic relations, its status has become very important. Therefore, the number of people traveling and surveying here every year is endless, traveling back and forth on the Ping-Sui

Page 20

road.

Because this place is close to desert areas in the north, southwest, the climate changes very drastically between hot and cold. In winter, it is of course very cold, and even in summer, it is often hot during the day and cold at night. Therefore, ordinary plants do not grow easily. The general production situation is also very backward. Most of the land is grassland that has not yet been cultivated, and only a small part is engaged in agriculture. The main production of the general public is to operate livestock using grasslands. In the livestock industry, the production of cattle and sheep is of course the main source, but horses also occupy a very important position. Therefore, the horses of Suiyuan are famous throughout the country.

Although most modern means of transportation are centered on machinery, in backward China, horses still occupy a very important position in transportation and farming. Especially in military affairs, its use is even more important. In order to encourage horse production and breed improvement, the Suiyuan provincial authorities hold a horse production competition every year to show their promotion. At each session, the counties of Suiyuan Province and the leagues and banners of Inner Mongolia enthusiastically participate, which forms a grand gathering of the Han and Mongolian ethnic groups once a year.

The horse production competition is held by the provincial government on the Double Ten Festival every year. The participating units, the counties and leagues and banners, first hold preliminary competitions within each unit to select the "horse selection line," and then gather in the provincial capital to participate in the competition. The competition venue is the Guihua County sports field in the Suiyuan provincial capital. Guihua County is divided into two cities, new and old, facing each other east and west, about five or six miles apart. This large sports field is in the middle of the two cities. Because of the climate, there are very few trees here, so this sports field is just a flat and huge wasteland. Few people usually come to this place to exercise, because besides the two grandstands built for horse racing and the simple horse racing track, there are no other facilities. However, the few days before and after the Double Ten Festival are different. Red men and green women, all the people in the city, gather here to watch this grand competition once a year. This is certainly because the people outside the Great Wall are particularly interested in horse racing, which is closely related to them, and there are few such opportunities to gather usually, which is also the main reason.

During the competition, local residents and Mongolians from various leagues and banners gather around the sports field, some riding horses, some taking cars, and some walking. In addition to the Han people, there are Manchus who speak fluent "Mandarin," Mongolians who drag their braids and wear purple robes, and what attracts the most attention are the Mongolian princes and noble women in Qing robes and jackets with pearl ornaments. This horse race has also become a human race exhibition at the same time.

The competition lasts for three days. If the weather is bad or the competition is not finished, it can be extended for a few days. Generally, the first two days are preliminary rounds, and the last day is the finals. There are different types of horses, generally divided into three types: running horses, trotting horses, and breeding horses. Running horses and trotting horses are trained to run or trot according to their nature from an early age. Breeding horses are young horses that have not yet matured. Competitions are also held separately according to these three categories.

The method of competition is to divide the various types of horses into groups and hold them individually. The starter and judges direct and evaluate. The distance for running horses and trotting horses is different. The distance for running horses is two li, while the distance for trotting horses is only one li. The time used for these two distances is generally between two minutes and fifteen seconds and two minutes and twenty-five seconds, and rarely exceeds two minutes and twenty-five seconds. However, this speed is considered quite impressive.

After the competition is over, prizes are awarded according to the rankings. Silver shields, winning flags, etc., are certainly included in the prizes, but most of them are saddles, stirrups, and the like. Sometimes the local authorities also give bonuses to the horse that runs first, or bestow excellent names such as "Sui Feng" [Sui Wind] or "Chi Dian" [Lightning].

Being good at riding horses is very common in nomadic life. Not only is this true for adults, but children are also very good at it. In one of the horse production competitions, one of the riders who won first place in the running horse race was only twelve or thirteen years old. Among us Mongolians, riding horses is even more common, and has almost become a daily necessity. Not to mention adults, it is also common for young men and women around fifteen years old to graze horses on one side of the grassland and chase each other while riding horses on the other side. They usually ride horses without saddles and reins, and they are also untrained wild horses. Often the boys ride horses and gallop past, and the girls grab the horse , turn around, mount the horse and chase after them. A natural picture is formed on the vast grassland.

In addition to being used for local transportation and farming, most of the horses produced here are sold to various armies in the country. Many people come here to purchase them every year. There are many horse shops in Guihua and Baotou. After the purchasers arrive here, there will be "horse dealers" to solicit business. All food and lodging are provided by the horse shop, and they will transport horses from all over the place for you to choose from.

There is no fixed price for horses. Ordinary untrained so-called wild horses are generally about forty or fifty yuan per horse. If they are trained and very good, the price is hard to say, ranging from several hundred to thousands of yuan. For example, "Sui Feng," which won first place in the running horse race at a certain horse race, was bought for a price of one thousand yuan. However, these horses are mostly noticed by wealthy people who love horses, and ordinary customers rarely inquire about them.

It also takes capital to graze horses here. In the spring, summer, and autumn seasons, it is of course possible to "graze green" on the grasslands, but in winter, it is necessary to purchase fodder to feed them. And the "Ba Tou" who manages the horse herd and the "horse master" who trains the horses must also be specialized talents, and their wages are also very considerable.

The scenery outside the Great Wall is fundamentally different from that in the interior. When the peach blossoms are red, the willows are green, and the birds are singing and the flowers are fragrant elsewhere, here the green grass is everywhere and the cattle and sheep are in flocks. The herdsmen hold long whips in their hands, perched high on horseback, shouting various calls to command the livestock herds. Coupled with the unique northerly wind outside the Great Wall and the distant bald mountains, a majestic picture is drawn! No wonder the poem "When the wind blows the grass low, the cattle and sheep appear" has become a famous line in history describing the scenery outside the Great Wall.

Cauterized Dates 210

— Lao Pu

Zhuoxian, Shanxi Correspondence

Zhuoxian County is famous for producing "cauterized dates." The so-called "cauterized dates" are baked with fire, crispy, sweet, and extremely delicious; they are sold in this province and North China, amounting to no less than several million yuan each year. About four thousand poor people in Zhuoxian County rely on this to make a living. Last year, the date harvest was abundant and sales were also strong, so most of those engaged in cauterized dates tripled their profits. The places where cauterized dates are made are commonly known as workshops; as long as you see various patterned signs made of hollow cauterized dates hanging at the entrance, it is a workshop for making cauterized dates. There are three hundred and several dozen of these workshops, most of which are concentrated in the western city area, and some are scattered in the four townships, but those are just some scattered small households. The date-making period is from the beginning of winter to the end of February of the following year, with only about four months of work; once spring arrives, due to climate conditions, they can no longer engage in baking.

The method of making dates is to build a stove about 15 feet long and 3 feet wide with earth bricks in an ordinary house, with five or six fire eyes dug on it. Then, hollow dates that have been pre-removed of their wooden pits are laid flat on a wire steel sheet and placed on top of the fire eyes for roasting. After a few minutes, they are moved once to make the heat even. After about an hour, the cauterized dates are ripe. This method seems simple at first glance, but no one dares to take on this task unless they are a skilled master with experience. According to insiders, when baking cauterized dates, if the placement is uneven or the heat is inaccurate when lighting the fire, the taste of the dates will be unpalatable. Therefore, those who take on this task are mostly the backbone figures of the workshop. Before the cauterized dates are baked, there is still a pitting procedure. This work is mostly done by women; each workshop employs about thirty women to remove the pits, and the daily wage is about 15 cents. In total, there are more than nine thousand women in each workshop removing pits. Therefore, in years of abundant date harvests, the livelihood of the general poor can be free from problems.

In the past, when transportation was underdeveloped, the cauterized dates, in addition to being supplied for consumption in the county, were transported to various counties for sale in old-fashioned wheelbarrows. The farthest sales only reached the border of this province; but in recent years, because transportation is not as obstructed as in the past, these types of cauterized dates are already sold in various parts of North China. Moreover, because cauterized dates were abundant last year, the price was extremely low. The price of first-class cauterized dates fell from about eight yuan to six yuan per hundred catties. As for second and third-class dates, they only sell for three or four yuan. Therefore, the strong sales of cauterized dates in Zhuoxian County this spring are a miracle rarely seen in previous years. In 1927, when Chuan Zuoyi was trapped in Zhuoxian County, he used cauterized dates to fill his stomach because the food supply had run out. He praised them greatly after eating them. It is said that this spring, he sent a secretary to Zhuoxian County and bought hundreds of catties of them.

— Qi

Price per copy: 5 cents, General Distributor: Life Bookstore

Because I wanted to gain some knowledge about health, I subscribed to a copy of "Healthy World" to read. The contents of this publication are indeed suitable for my needs. This should be meaningful to general friends who hope for health.

This text is a continuation of the previous issue - the fourth issue. These articles are also worth reading carefully. It can tell you some sexual knowledge, it can make you know some rules on how to exercise your body, it can make you get some pathological and scientific common sense, which can cope with the arrival of certain diseases.

In addition, there are some small things, such as "Healthy Maxims," such as "A Bundle of Strange News" including "Mother and Daughter Fighting for Property," "New Zealand Hurricane," "Hail in South Africa Like Cannonballs"... These articles are also worth noting and are interesting.

Economic Exchange

Recent Overview of Global Rubber Production and Consumption 212

— 品成

During the economic panic, all commodities showed a severe state of overproduction, and rubber, the most widely used and produced commodity, could not escape this fate. Therefore, in June of the year before last, the major rubber-producing countries of the world established the International Rubber Restriction Agreement to limit rubber production. Last year, some people in Southeast Asia even advocated a weekly rest, claiming that this measure had several benefits: "First, based on the natural fundamental law of permanent success; second, fair treatment for both European and local rubber companies, large and small; third, as a fundamental restriction method to balance supply and demand, benefiting both the physical and mental well-being of vehicle owners and workers, the physiological principle of metabolism is also beneficial to rubber, and rubber production should increase accordingly." In fact, the fundamental meaning of this proposal, in a nutshell, is simply an attempt to further restrict rubber production in Southeast Asia. Under such artificial production restrictions, the global rubber market has indeed shown a relatively positive trend recently. At the same time, due to the enthusiastic expansion of armaments by various countries in recent years, especially the resulting boom in the automotive industry, the global demand for rubber has also increased rapidly. Thus, with production restrictions on one hand and increased demand on the other, the result is naturally a relative improvement in the rubber market.

In reality, the stock of rubber held by major rubber-producing countries around the world has been decreasing day by day in the past year and this year. For example, the United States, mainly due to its own increased demand, saw its rubber stock decrease by approximately 60,000 tons last year. In addition, in the United Kingdom, rubber stock had increased to 177,000 tons by the end of September last year, but it decreased to 162,000 tons by the end of January this year. In the Straits Settlements and Malaya, a review of the situation in recent years shows that rubber stocks have also tended to decrease relatively. Now, to better understand the issue, we can present the following statistics on the recent state of rubber stocks around the world (unit: thousands of tons):

Based on the table above, we can see that: compared to 1933, world rubber consumption increased by 109,000 tons in 1934, but production increased even more, by 136,000 tons. As a result, world rubber production in 1933 exceeded consumption (overproduction) by 59,000 tons, and in 1934 it exceeded consumption by even more, 86,000 tons. However, compared to 1934, world rubber consumption increased by only 10,000 tons in 1935, but because production decreased by 150,000 tons, the result was a supply shortage of 74,000 tons, with consumption exceeding production. This is clearly due to the establishment of the International Rubber Restriction Agreement in 1934, which limited rubber production.

However, many contradictions have also emerged within the international rubber restriction. The most obvious is the difficulty in controlling the rubber exports of local people in the Dutch East Indies. This is because: first, without conducting surveys or land registrations of local rubber plantations, it is impossible to proportionally restrict the exports of each producer; second, the International Restriction Agreement stipulates too small a proportion for the rubber exports of local people in the Dutch East Indies. According to the provisions of the restriction agreement, the permitted export volume of local rubber in 1935 was 112,516 tons, but actual production was three to four times greater than this. Given these difficulties in controlling exports, the rubber exports of local people in the Dutch East Indies have actually exceeded the permitted volume in recent years, as follows—

The Dutch East Indies government is naturally very distressed by this situation. Without a way to limit the increase in local production and exports, the Dutch East Indies government requested an increase in the export quota for local people in the first phase of last year, but because the world's rubber stocks were still trending upward at that time, the request was not approved by the various producing countries. As a result, the Dutch East Indies government could only continue to attack the local people, repeatedly increasing export taxes. Until the end of last year, due to the artificial improvement of the global rubber market, the International Rubber Control Committee substantially increased the export volume of the Dutch East Indies at its regular meeting in November, and also substantially increased the export quota for local people in the Dutch East Indies. However, because all situations are caused by artificially restricting production, the problem remains fundamentally unresolved.

Some people estimate, based on past situations, that world rubber consumption this year will be approximately 1.04 million tons, averaging 83,700 tons per month. Among these, the consumption volume of various countries in the world is roughly as follows (unit: thousands of tons)——

Based on this estimate, world rubber stocks may continue to decrease this year, and the rubber market may continue to improve.

Page 21

However, restrictions on rubber production will first affect the lives of workers. Taking the situation in the Dutch East Indies as an example, before the implementation of rubber restrictions, rubber workers earned more than one yuan per day, and there was a shortage of workers. However, after the implementation of rubber restrictions, various rubber plantations had to dismiss workers one after another, and at the same time reduce wages. As a result, some rubber workers had to leave their workplaces and seek other livelihoods, while others faced greater financial pressure due to reduced wages. Consequently, peddlers and even general stores in various rubber-producing areas lost a large number of customers, further deepening the market depression. Based on this manifestation, we can see that artificially restricting rubber production, creating an improvement in the rubber market, has resulted in affecting other industries in society, deepening the depression in other industries, and making the lives of most laborers more painful and impoverished. Therefore, in the final analysis, the recent situation of rubber production and consumption is still a distorted phenomenon generated within the current deformed world economic situation.

Illustrated Spring and Autumn

Review of the Inaugural Issue of "Nightingale" 213

— 香草

Currently, besides the established "Literature," there are hardly any other literary publications to be seen. "Nightingale" is a small-scale literary publication. Judging from its inaugural issue, each section is evenly distributed, and it is no exaggeration to say that the content is rich.

However, none of the five essays grasp reality – none address issues beneficial to the country or the nation; Mr. Tang Tao's "On 'Extraordinary Times'" is relatively more meaningful, but it only speaks in vague terms. Of course, the barbarity of people like Fu ×× should be condemned, but it is not as cruel as the invasion of imperialism!

In terms of creative writing, Mr. Wang Renshu's "Mist" depicts the tragic lives of Chinese farmers from a lateral perspective. Farmers cannot make a living, so they take joining the army as a "way out," but being a soldier is far from their ideals, so they want to "escape," but where can they escape to? "Return to their hometown"? But "those who guard the fields are starving," in a word, "cannot escape death"! Therefore, dogs eating human flesh is commonplace. Currently, at a time when the nation is dying, we urgently need heroes of resolute determination, but we do not need heroes who fight among themselves. This piece is a complete work both in terms of meaning and technique. Mr. Zhuang Qidong's "Unemployed" focuses on describing the psychology of unemployed people seeking jobs, but after "hitting a wall," it does not leave him with the necessary awareness, and it is too simplistic to be considered a story. Mr. Fang Zhizhong's "A Group of Rebellious Women" is a reportage style piece. He singles out the daughter of a staff officer as the protagonist among a group of women, and makes that supposedly typical figure, Liu Ge Fei, play a supporting role, perhaps with his own intentions. I have discovered two characteristics in many of the author's works: first, he uses venomous strokes to ridicule the characters he dislikes; second, he mixes the characters' personalities into their actions and words. In addition, he also uses cartoon-like techniques to promote the development of the story. This piece still maintains this style. As for the evaluation of its significance to the times, the readers will know for themselves. Among the three essays, Mr. Dong Ping's "The Prophecy of the Saint" seems like a fable, the writing is too ornate, which blurs the meaning. Xi Ru's "From Ningjin to Shijiazhuang" can only be considered a travelogue. Luo Feng's "Beggar with a Violin" writes about a White Russian vagrant in Harbin, reminiscing about the luxury of the past and lamenting the cruelty of reality. I remember that Jiang Guangci once wrote "Lisa's Lament" on this theme, because the sentimental tone towards the protagonist was too heavy, the result was that he became her sympathizer. In this article, the author also committed the same mistake. Bai Shu and Shi Yu are two young poets, so their passion and righteous indignation are surging and pulsating in their poems, which is vastly different from the modernists and New Crescent School who decorate from the words. Both theoretical articles are translations, but the former is exactly the "Comforto" of the Chinese literary world today. There was a time in the Chinese literary world when the prejudice that content was more important than form prevailed, and what is the relationship between form and content? This article tells us everything. The latter is translated too awkwardly, and the problem also seems not very important. Introducing the anti-war writer Tolstoy, I think this is very important, although Tolstoy is a well-known writer to Chinese youth. Now the situation in all of Europe and the Far East has reached the most dangerous moment, and the most cruel second human massacre is about to appear before us. There is no doubt that we need great writers like Tolstoy. Mr. Yong Zhong's "Discussion After Reading Lu Xun's 'Old Tales Retold'" is just as the author said himself, "not a critic," "if anyone wants to treat it as criticism, 'it is bound to be disappointed.'" There are too few critics in China, and even fewer fair critics. The task of critics is to point out the advantages and disadvantages of works, so that appreciators can appreciate and later learners can learn or be warned. But Chinese critics (to put it mildly) either blindly praise or scold, fair criticism is rare, which is really the most serious problem in the Chinese literary world today.

Biographies of Famous People

Medical Scholar Jules Bordet 214

— 桀人

Jules Bordet was not only a famous and great medical scholar in Belgium, but also a figure worthy of special attention in the modern world of medicine. In 1919, he won the Nobel Prize in Medicine, and since then his achievements in medicine have spread even further around the world, and he himself has become a truly international medical scholar.

This great medical scholar was born in Soignies, Belgium, on June 13, 1870. He is currently a professor of bacteriology, parasitology, and epidemiology at the University of Brussels, and also the director of the Bruserpasteur Institut. He not only possesses the technical knowledge of a general physician, but also has in-depth research on the theories of physiology, medicine, and especially epidemiology. His appearance is very amiable, and at first glance, one can see that he is a gentle and studious scholar. However, we have no way to examine his childhood life, and it seems that there is not much need for examination, so now, the main goal is to introduce his research and its results, which should be more meaningful.

Dr. Bordet's most important research includes three aspects: the phenomenon of hemolysis, the phenomenon of complement fixation, and the discovery of the pertussis bacillus. He began his research in 1895, when he was already twenty-five years old. The year before, the German Faffel had discovered that cholera bacteria dissolved and disappeared in the abdominal cavity of guinea pigs. This is known as the Faffel reaction in medical science. Bordet naturally paid special attention to this matter, and after conducting his own practical experiments, he learned that this phenomenon was due to the action of guinea pig serum. According to his experiments, if cholera bacteria were used to perform immunization treatment, it would not be limited to guinea pigs, and the serum of other animals could also dissolve cholera bacteria.

It was in this experiment that Bordet grasped the essence of immunity. He paid special attention to red blood cells. The results of his experiments were that if red blood cells from animal A were injected into animal B instead of bacteria to perform so-called immunization treatment, then the serum of animal B would show the ability to dissolve the blood cells of animal A. This is called hemolysis. This type of experiment uses red blood cells to replace pathogenic bacteria, so there is no danger at all, and the experimental method is also very simple. The effectiveness can be clearly demonstrated within one or two hours. Dr. Bordet then gradually completed the analysis and research of the immune phenomenon. To say that the current theory of immunology originated from his research is not an exaggeration.

In the above-mentioned hemolysis, there are two substances at play. One is expressed in the serum of the new animal through immunization treatment, which Dr. Bordet named sensitizer (Substance sensibilisnforius). The other has a direct effect of dissolving red blood cells, and exists in the serum of ordinary animals; this substance is called Alexin. Serum therapy, as we usually say, is a method of treating the human body by injecting the serum of immunized animals. In this way, the so-called immunity should be understandable.

After Dr. Bordet published the phenomenon of hemolysis, the German Ehrlich followed up with research on this issue. His views differed in many ways from Bordet's, so they engaged in a great debate, which is a matter worthy of special attention in the academic field of the late nineteenth century.

Dr. Bordet believes that the Alexin that plays the main role in the dissolution of cholera bacteria and the Alexin in the dissolution of red blood cells are the same substance (at this time, Alexin had been renamed Complement), so he paid special attention to this issue: that is, if the complement is eliminated once in order to dissolve cholera bacteria, then even if red blood cells are added at this point, the dissolution phenomenon will not occur. Then

Continue on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

He applied this complement fixation and discovered the pertussis bacillus; the greatness of the quality of his research can be said to have truly manifested from this point onward.

After Dr. Bordet applied complement fixation and discovered the pertussis bacillus, the German physician Wassermann used it to perform syphilis diagnosis, and thus Wassermann's reputation spread throughout the world. But according to knowledgeable people, Bordet's reputation is pure gold in terms of academics, while Wassermann's reputation is merely gilded.

Now, we can also briefly talk about the pertussis bacillus discovered by Dr. Bordet. The so-called spasm can be said to be a type of neurological disease; the state of this disease is the rapid contraction of muscles, that is, the general term commonly known as muscle cramps. Those who suffer from this disease are mostly children. The disease can be either mild or severe. In severe cases, it can end a small life within a few hours; and the disease is quite contagious, so it is very dangerous. However, the pathogen of this acute infectious disease in children has always been unknown, until Dr. Bordet discovered that a type of bacteria was cultivated in the throat of children suffering from this disease. However, it is difficult to present evidence for this discovery, because in fact, one cannot take a living child to experiment. Therefore, Dr. Bordet applied the above-mentioned complement fixation product to test it. The pertussis bacillus he cultivated was able to clearly prove the cause of pertussis by applying this complement diversion effect. His discovery has been recognized by scholars around the world; at the same time, due to his discovery, the prevention and treatment of so-called spasmodic diseases have established a certain effective approach. This is truly a great contribution to mankind.

Dr. Bordet has a son-in-law named Gengou, who is also a profound medical researcher and scientist. He is Dr. Bordet's assistant, and he worked hard on the research of hemolysis and pertussis bacteria; he certainly also provided great help to the doctor's research. He is currently a technician at the Belgian Health Bureau, very active, and his future achievements are immeasurable.

Finally, I would also like to report a piece of news: Dr. Bordet, whom we are talking about here, has been elected as the honorary president of the Second International Society for Bacteriology and Biology, which will be held in London in July this year. Just from this point of view, the doctor's reputation and status in the international medical and scientific communities can be fully imagined.

Amateur Cafe

"Thirty Years Later" 215

— 柳湜

Recently, relying on a bit of youthful vigor, I carried out an action to break superstitions in my hometown, because in that city circle, like other city circles, there are always quite a few idle gentlemen. In order to pass the idle days, I don't know if it was due to "inspiration from outside the sky," they were fascinated by the mad monk Ji Gong, set up a spirit altar, and allowed the general ignorant men and women to inquire about karma and seek treatment for diseases, and surprisingly their "business was booming." But later, the behavior of those old gentlemen became more and more absurd, so we submitted a request to the county government to ban it, but it was rumored on the streets that the spirit channeling organization would soon be converted into a Buddhist branch. In fact, religion and superstition are by no means one and the same. Although we have no prejudice against religion, we firmly oppose superstition. In order to understand the truth of this matter, I specially went to ask the host of the Buddhist branch, a certain master of Chinese studies, and he sincerely told us: he did not participate in the spirit altar, but said: "Thirty years ago, I also tried hard to break superstitions, but the vast and subtle nature of Buddhism has recently made me dare not say a word." I couldn't help but shudder when I heard these words, "Thirty years ago," what a terrible period this is!

The question here is: Why did they try as hard as we did to break superstitions thirty years ago? Why couldn't the vast and subtle nature of Buddhism be discovered thirty years ago, but had to be discovered thirty years later?

I know what that master of Chinese studies means: you should not rely solely on youthful vigor to make a fuss about breaking superstitions. I am afraid that you will also be silent and no longer speak thirty years later. If my guess is correct, then I will be very grateful for his kindness. This is a lesson from the past.

There is also an old story in our hometown, saying that a certain young man learned martial arts from a boxer for three years, and thought that his skills were extraordinary and invincible. One day, the village was performing a community opera. There is a custom of "squeezing the head stage" in the countryside, which means relying on one's own strength to squeeze to the front of the stage to watch the opera. Those without strength can only stand behind the heads of people and cannot get a good position, so young people with strength and face in the countryside often have to squeeze the head stage. Of course, this young warrior also had to squeeze to the front of the stage, but he didn't know that the warrior who thought he was invincible was knocked down by another person with greater strength. He was very frustrated, very awakened, and knew that his strength was not enough, so he closed his doors to cultivate himself, sought another famous teacher, and studied for another three years. His skills became higher, but his self-confidence gradually disappeared, and he did not dare to move his fists and feet arbitrarily. The old people often used this story as a material to teach us, and also recited a jingle: "Three years of initial learning, can go everywhere, three years of further learning, difficult to move an inch." That master of Chinese studies probably thought of himself as a person who had "studied for another three years," and of course, our breaking of superstitions was just a greenhorn who had "studied for three years."

The above story cannot actually be used as a metaphor for our breaking of superstitions, because it is specious. Learning for three more years, recognizing that there is greater knowledge and skills in the world, making him feel that his academic skills are insufficient and striving to learn, this is indeed correct, but if, for the sake of the vast and subtle content of Buddhism, using a blurred gaze to look up at the towering giant, thinking that he will never be able to touch his head, and thus daring not to break superstitions, this is really not a true feeling of the profundity of the Buddhist party's content, but a symbol of old age, blood decay, and lack of courage!

China is a nation that decays early. Before reaching old age, they already hold a playful attitude towards the world. There is also a type of young people who "decay before old age," and hold a reclusive attitude like the elderly. The "thirty years ago" mentioned by that master of Chinese studies may still be considered a slightly distant time. Looking around, the sea has changed for ten years, and I am afraid it has already turned into mulberry fields! Many of the great men who made revolution thirty years ago have actually felt the vast and subtle nature of Buddhism and converted to Buddhism today after thirty years. As for us, we are probably still people of the "thirty years ago" era. I don't know if we will also convert to Buddha, convert to Dharma, and convert to Sangha in the "thirty years later" era?

Literary Works

Brother's Happy Event (End) 216

— 益

"No accidents happened today, it can be said that we have fulfilled our responsibility to protect." He proudly surveyed everyone once, "However, the battalion commander has ordered me to take back the donation－－" He stared at me with force in his eyes, "Eighty yuan."

The words "donation" and the number were said especially brightly. I don't quite understand the situation in the countryside and don't know how to answer. But happily, my second brother went up and said very seriously:

"Officer, our 'wedding wine donation' has already been paid sixty yuan."

"The wedding wine donation is the wedding wine donation, this is the 'protection donation.'"

"We didn't ask anyone to protect us, and there's no such thing as a 'donation'," my second brother said angrily.

The platoon leader's face sank, and he immediately showed a ferocious expression:

"I don't care, this is 'official business'."

"Bird's 'official business', clearly fraud..."

Before the platoon leader finished speaking, he slapped him in the face, and then said sharply:

"Are you going to take it or not?"

At this time, my second brother didn't know where the energy came from, and suddenly rushed forward, speaking in a decisive tone:

"There is no money, you can take my life if you want!"

The platoon leader pulled his slanted belt, raised his pistol with his right hand, "Okay! You dare to resist official business." Then he tilted his head and said to the soldiers next to him, "Come! Tie him back to the town!"

So a few wolf-like soldiers immediately grabbed my second brother, and the rest aimed their guns as if they were about to shoot. The timid guests hurried back to avoid them, and the family members were watching from the door with their hands and feet clenched. I know that the ending of this matter is not serious, but it will always cost a few dollars to settle the matter. So I persuaded my second brother to stop, and asked the platoon leader not to be angry. The bolder guests also came to help say good things, and the platoon leader allowed him not to be taken away, but the money had to be paid immediately. As a result, after our repeated requests, it seemed like settling a homicide case, and only then did we agree to a "donation" of thirty yuan, plus ten yuan for the soldiers' cigarette and tea expenses. In the end, my mother mournfully brought out forty yuan, which I gave to the platoon leader. He counted the amount and said very peacefully:

"This is the battalion commander's order, the brothers are just doing their duty."

After the soldier masters took the money away, everyone in the family was like they had lost their souls. My second brother fell weakly on the bamboo chair, his chest rising and falling as if his breathing was about to stop!

Soon the sky became dark, and my brother's happy event sank into the darkness!

Random Jottings 217

— Zhuo Er

Silent iron is a piece of scrap iron.

A thief says: I used the thought of "others steal even more fiercely than I do" to comfort my conscience.

A clever person, when drunk, becomes doubly clever.

A person who has had smallpox, even if recovered, always has scars.

Only when the dim twilight secretly begins to creep into life can one feel that the spring storm is the freshest and most precious.

Silver Screen Jottings 219

— Zhi Er

Old Cai wrote to a friend saying: "A Lost Sheep" is almost finished filming, but the closing procedures still need some time. - Although few scenes were filmed, he has not wasted a single day.

At the Yangtze Dance Hall's banquet for the press, "Revolutionary" Huang Tian did not arrive in a Zhongshan suit, which was disappointing. Someone wanted to dance "Revolutionary Object," but it was cancelled because he was not wearing a Zhongshan suit.

The names of the forty founders of the Film Industry Association have been signed. The actor representatives who signed were Hu Die for Mingxing, Gao Zhanfei, Chen Yanyan and Li Zhuozhuo for Lianhua, and Wang Yin and Yuan Meiyun for Yihua.

Hopefully, the Film Industry Association will live to be a hundred years old and not become like tea parties, where the venue gets higher and higher and the number of people gets smaller and smaller. And hopefully, it will do some real "association" work.
